## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermomechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is the standard setting for constitutive laws in solids (elasticity, plasticity, creep) with thermal expansion and temperature-dependent stiffness/strength. Typical relationships combine an elastic response in epsilon with temperature-dependent modulus, yield stress, and thermally activated flow/softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear thermoelasticity (thermal strain offset): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * (epsilon - c2 * (T - c3)) (small-strain elastic stress including thermal expansion)
- Hooke-type with temperature-dependent modulus (softening/stiffening): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (temperature-dependent Young’s modulus, low strain)
- Exponential modulus decay with temperature: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (thermally softened elastic modulus)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial (Landau-type expansion): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**3 (weak nonlinearity at moderate strain)
- Ramberg–Osgood-style inversion surrogate: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon / (c2 + Abs(epsilon)**c3) (smooth transition from linear to nonlinear compliance; empirical)
- Power-law strain hardening with temperature-dependent strength: sigma = (c0 * exp(-c1 * T)) * (Abs(epsilon) + c2)**c3 * sign(epsilon) (plastic-like hardening with thermal softening; symmetric in tension/compression)
- Ludwik/Hollomon hardening form with offset strain: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) + (c2 * exp(-c3 * T)) * (Abs(epsilon) + c4)**c5 (yield-like offset plus strain hardening; temperature reduces strength)
- Voce-type saturation hardening (strain-controlled): sigma = (c0 * exp(-c1 * T)) + c2 * (1 - exp(-c3 * Abs(epsilon))) * sign(epsilon) (saturating hardening towards a plateau)
- Thermal softening multiplier (Johnson–Cook-like without strain rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2) * (1 - c3 * (T - c4)**c5) (empirical plasticity with melting/softening trend)
- Eyring/thermal-activation-inspired stress–strain surrogate: sigma = (c0 * exp(-c1 * T)) * asinh(c2 * epsilon) (smoothly transitions from linear to logarithmic growth; thermally activated flow proxy)
- Creep/viscoplastic power law in strain with Arrhenius-like temperature factor (strain-as-time proxy): sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) * (Abs(epsilon) + c2)**c3 * sign(epsilon) (empirical when epsilon correlates with accumulated creep/flow at a given T)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic (yield at temperature-dependent level): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon for Abs(epsilon) <= c2 + c3 * T; else sigma = (c4 * exp(-c5 * T)) + c6 * (Abs(epsilon) - (c2 + c3 * T))**c7 * sign(epsilon) (elastic regime then plastic hardening; yield shifts with T)
- Hyperelastic-like (neo-Hookean small-strain surrogate): sigma = (c0 * exp(-c1 * T)) * (epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2) (rubberlike/large-strain-inspired curvature with thermal softening)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Elastic regime identification: sigma approximately linear in epsilon at small |epsilon|, suggesting leading term (temperature-dependent) * epsilon.
- Thermal expansion effect: subtracting a term like c * (T - T0) from epsilon models stress-free thermal strain and produces sigma≈0 along a temperature-dependent epsilon offset.
- Temperature-dependent stiffness: E(T) commonly decreases with T; structures like exp(-c*T) or low-order polynomials in T multiplying epsilon capture this.
- Yield/strength softening with temperature: multiplicative softening factors (1 - c*(T - T0)^n) or exp(-c*T) applied to a hardening law represent reduced flow stress at higher T.
- Hardening saturation: terms like 1 - exp(-c*|epsilon|) encode approach to a stress plateau (Voce-type), common in metals after some plastic strain.
- Symmetry considerations: if the material response is similar in tension/compression, using Abs(epsilon) with an explicit sign(epsilon) factor can represent odd stress–strain symmetry.
- Smooth elastic-to-plastic transition: rational forms in epsilon (e.g., epsilon/(c+|epsilon|^n)) emulate changing tangent modulus without a sharp yield point.
- Thermally activated flow signatures: logarithmic/asinh dependence on epsilon (with temperature prefactors) can mimic activation-controlled deformation where stress increases slowly at large strain.
- Coupled T–epsilon interaction: cross-terms like T*epsilon or T*epsilon^n often represent that strain sensitivity (hardening rate) itself changes with temperature.

Now let me check candidates with epsilon*exp(T*c) type terms, which could potentially give T*epsilon**3 through Taylor expansion - NO, we can't use approximations.

Actually, let me reconsider. Can any candidate with exp terms match? The GT is purely polynomial in T and epsilon. An exp(T*c) term with c≠0 can never be polynomial. So any candidate relying on exp(T*c) for the T*epsilon**3 coupling cannot match unless c=0, reducing it to a constant.

Let me check candidates that have explicit T*epsilon**3 or T*(epsilon+c)³:

Only Candidates 4, 12, 13, 14, 17, 31 have this.

**Candidate 4 revisited:** `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon**3 + c2*epsilon + c3*epsilon**c4 + c5*epsilon**3`

Set c2=0, c4=0 (then c3*epsilon^0 = c3, a constant):
T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon**3 + c3 + c5*epsilon**3

This gives: T, T*epsilon**3, constant, epsilon**3 ✓ All four basis functions!

Wait, if c4=0, then epsilon**c4 = epsilon**0 = 1, so c3*epsilon**c4 = c3. Yes!

GT = c0*T + c1*T*epsilon**3 + c3 + c5*epsilon**3. This matches!

Candidate 4 verdict: [MATCH]

Now let me continue checking the remaining candidates more carefully.

**Candidate 1:** `T*c0*epsilon/(c1 + Abs(epsilon)**c2) + c3*epsilon*exp(T*c4) + c5 + c6*Abs(epsilon)**4 + c7*epsilon/(c1 + Abs(epsilon)**c2)`

For ε≥0: T*c0*ε/(c1+ε^c2) + c3*ε*exp(T*c4) + c5 + c6*ε⁴ + c7*ε/(c1+ε^c2)

The term c3*ε*exp(T*c4) can't give polynomial T dependence unless c4=0 → c3*ε.
The rational terms: (T*c0+c7)*ε/(c1+ε^c2). If c2=1: (T*c0+c7)*ε/(c1+ε) - this is rational, not polynomial.
If c1=0, c2=2: (T*c0+c7)*ε/ε² = (T*c0+c7)/ε - singular.
If c1=0, c2=1: (T*c0+c7)*ε/ε = T*c0+c7 - constant + T term.

Wait, if c1=0 and c2=1: ε/(0+ε) = 1. Then T*c0 + c7 + c3*ε + c5 + c6*ε⁴.
Basis: T, constant, ε, ε⁴. Missing T*ε³ and ε³.

If c2=4, c1=0: ε/ε⁴ = 1/ε³ - bad.
If c2=0, c1≠0: ε/(c1+1) = const*ε. Still no T*ε³.

No way to get T*epsilon**3.

Candidate 1 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 2:** `T*c0 + T*c1*epsilon/(c2 + Abs(epsilon)**c3) + c4*exp(c5*epsilon) + c6*epsilon/(c2 + Abs(epsilon)**c3) + c7 + c8*(c9 + Abs(epsilon))**4`

T*c1*ε/(c2+ε^c3): rational in ε, can't produce T*ε³ as polynomial unless special cases.
If c2=0, c3=1: T*c1*ε/ε = T*c1. Just T.
If c2=0, c3=-2: T*c1*ε/ε^(-2) = T*c1*ε³. This gives T*ε³!

With c2=0, c3=-2: c6*ε/ε^(-2) = c6*ε³.
Set c4=0 (kill exp).
(c9+ε)⁴ expansion: need c8=0 to avoid ε⁴ etc.

Then: T*c0 + T*c1*ε³ + c6*ε³ + c7
Basis: T, T*ε³, ε³, constant ✓

But wait, c3=-2 means Abs(epsilon)**c3 = epsilon^(-2). Is this valid? The expression c2+|ε|^c3 with c2=0 becomes |ε|^(-2) = 1/ε². Then ε/(1/ε²) = ε³. Yes, this works for ε>0 (not at ε=0, but that's a measure-zero point).

Candidate 2 verdict: [MATCH]

**Candidate 3:** `T*c0 + c1*epsilon + c2*epsilon**3 + c3*Max(0, T*c4 + c5 + Abs(epsilon))**4`

The Max term is problematic. For it to produce T*epsilon**3, we'd need the Max to be active and expand. But (T*c4+c5+ε)⁴ contains T⁴ terms which can't be canceled. Unless c4=0: Max(0, c5+ε)⁴ = (c5+ε)⁴ (if c5+ε≥0), which has no T dependence.
If c3=0: T*c0 + c1*ε + c2*ε³. Missing T*ε³ and constant.

Candidate 3 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 5:** `T*c0 + c1*exp(c2*epsilon) + c3 + c4*(c5 + Abs(epsilon))**4 + c6*log(c7*exp(T*c8 + c9*epsilon) + 1)`

The log term: log(c7*exp(T*c8+c9*ε)+1). This is a softplus-like function. It can't be polynomial in T. If c6=0, then T*c0 + c1*exp(c2*ε) + c3 + c4*(c5+ε)⁴. No T*ε³.

Candidate 5 verdict: [NO MATCH]

**Candidate 6:** `c0*epsilon*exp(T*c1) + c2 + c3*log(c4*epsilon + 1) + c5*Abs(epsilon)**4 + c6*(c7 + Abs(epsilon))**2*exp(c8/T)`

exp(T*c1) and exp(c8/T) can't produce polynomial T. If c0=0, c6=0: c2 + c3*log(c4*ε+1) + c5*ε⁴. No T dependence at all (except if we keep c0 or c6 nonzero, but then we get exp terms).

All T-dependent terms are exponential in T. Can't produce T*ε³.
